<table role="presentation" class="metadata mbox-small noprint selfref" style="border:1px solid #aaa;background-color:#f9f9f9;width: 22em;">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Uyghurche.png/40px-Uyghurche.png" width="40" height="18" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Uyghurche.png/60px-Uyghurche.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Uyghurche.png/80px-Uyghurche.png 2x" data-file-width="287" data-file-height="131" /></td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="vertical-align:middle; font-size:95%;"><b>This article contains <a href="/wiki/Uyghur_Arabic_alphabet" title="Uyghur Arabic alphabet">Uyghur text</a>.</b> Without proper <a href="/wiki/Help:Arabic" title="Help:Arabic">rendering support</a>, you may see unjoined letters running left to right or other symbols instead of <a href="/wiki/Uyghur_Arabic_alphabet" title="Uyghur Arabic alphabet">Uyghur script</a>.</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><b>Ürümqi</b> (<a href="/wiki/Simplified_Chinese_characters" title="Simplified Chinese characters">Chinese</a>: <span lang="zh-Hans" xml:lang="zh-Hans">乌鲁木齐</span>; <a href="/wiki/Pinyin" title="Pinyin">pinyin</a>: <i><span lang="zh-Latn-pinyin" xml:lang="zh-Latn-pinyin">Wūlǔmùqí</span></i>, <a href="/wiki/Uyghur_language" title="Uyghur language">Uyghur</a>: <span lang="ug-Arab" xml:lang="ug-Arab">ئۈرۈمچى</span>‎; from <a href="/wiki/Oirat_language" title="Oirat language">Oirat</a> "beautiful pasture") is the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Xinjiang" title="Xinjiang">Xinjiang Uyghur Autonomous Region</a> of the <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">People's Republic of China</a><sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> in <a href="/wiki/Northwest_China" title="Northwest China">Northwest China</a>. Ürümqi was a major hub on the <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">Silk Road</a> during China's <a href="/wiki/Tang_dynasty" title="Tang dynasty">Tang dynasty</a>, and developed its reputation as a leading cultural and commercial center during the <a href="/wiki/Qing_dynasty" title="Qing dynasty">Qing dynasty</a>.</p>
<p>With a built-up (<i>or metro</i>) population of 2,988,715 as of 2010<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> census (6 urban and suburban districts but Dabancheng not yet urbanized) and 3.03 million in 7 urban and suburban districts,<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> Ürümqi is the largest city in China's western interior. Since the 1990s Ürümqi has developed economically and serves as a regional transport <a href="/wiki/List_of_transport_topics#Nodes" class="mw-redirect" title="List of transport topics">node</a>, cultural, and commercial center.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_period">Early period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Although Ürümqi is situated near the northern route of the <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">Silk Road</a>, the present city is a relatively young city. It was not called Urumqi until the time of the <a href="/wiki/Dzungar_Khanate" title="Dzungar Khanate">Dzungar Khanate</a>. An older settlement was located nearby – according to Chinese scholars, during the 22nd year of <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Taizong_of_Tang" title="Emperor Taizong of Tang">Emperor Taizong</a>'s reign in the <a href="/wiki/Tang_dynasty" title="Tang dynasty">Tang dynasty</a>, AD 648, the Tang government set up the town of <b>Luntai</b> in the ancient town seat of Urabo,<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> 10 kilometres (6 miles) from the southern suburb of present-day Ürümqi in the Tang dynasty's <a href="/wiki/Protectorate_General_to_Pacify_the_West" title="Protectorate General to Pacify the West">Protectorate General to Pacify the West</a> which controlled Xinjiang. Ancient Luntai Town was a seat of local government, and collected taxes from the <a href="/wiki/Caravan_(travellers)" title="Caravan (travellers)">caravans</a> along the northern route of the Silk Road. After the Tang retreated from the <a href="/wiki/Western_Regions" title="Western Regions">Western Regions</a>, the region came under the control of the <a href="/wiki/Uyghurs" title="Uyghurs">Uyghurs</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Uyghur_Khaganate" title="Uyghur Khaganate">Khaganate</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gaochang" title="Gaochang">Gaochang</a>/<a href="/wiki/Qocho" class="mw-redirect" title="Qocho">Qocho</a>. Between the Tang until the Qing, there was little information about the Ürümqi area, and there appeared to be no permanent settlement here for some time. The Mongols referred to the wider area as <a href="/wiki/Beshbalik" class="mw-redirect" title="Beshbalik">Bishbalik</a> meaning five cities, referring to the five towns that surrounded the present-day Ürümqi area.<sup id="cite_ref-piper_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-piper-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dzungar_period">Dzungar period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Dzungar period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Oirats" title="Oirats">Oirats</a> <a href="/wiki/Dzungar_people" title="Dzungar people">Dzungar</a> tribes that formed the <a href="/wiki/Dzungar_Khanate" title="Dzungar Khanate">Dzungar Khanate</a> were the last major power to control Ürümqi before the Manchus gained control of Xinjiang, and their language gave Ürümqi its modern-day name. In the Ming dynasty, there was a record of a place at Jiujiawan 5 kilometres (3 miles) to the west of present Ürümqi, which may have been the Dzunghar town that was later destroyed during the Qing conquest. The Mongolians also used the area as herding ground in this period.<sup id="cite_ref-piper_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-piper-4">[4]</a></sup> Steppe peoples had used the location, the pass between the <a href="/wiki/Bogda_Shan" title="Bogda Shan">Bogda Shan</a> to the east and the <a href="/wiki/Tian_Shan" title="Tian Shan">Tian Shan</a> to the west, connecting the <a href="/wiki/Dzungaria" title="Dzungaria">Dzungar Basin</a> to the north and the <a href="/wiki/Turpan_Depression" title="Turpan Depression">Turpan Depression</a> to the south.</p>
<p>Ürümqi remained a small town, and less important than the oasis and Silk Road trade center <a href="/wiki/Turpan" title="Turpan">Turpan</a> 200&#160;km (120&#160;mi) to the southeast. Fighting for the control of Dzungaria led to the <a href="/wiki/Khoshut" title="Khoshut">Khoshuuts</a> (now classified as Mongols) leaving Ürümqi for Qinghai and Tibet in the 1620s an 1630s.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> The Uyghurs were introduced into the Ürümqi area in the 18th century by the Dzunghars who moved them from the west Tarim region to be <i>taranchis</i> or farmers in Ürümqi.<sup id="cite_ref-Millward2007_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Millward2007-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Qing_rule">Qing rule</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Qing rule">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the 18th century, the Qing went to war against the <a href="/wiki/Dzungar_Khanate" title="Dzungar Khanate">Dzungar Khanate</a>. Ürümqi was taken by the Qing in 1755, and the Dzungars of the region were eliminated in the <a href="/wiki/Dzungar_genocide" title="Dzungar genocide">Dzungar genocide</a>. One writer, <a href="/wiki/Wei_Yuan" title="Wei Yuan">Wei Yuan</a>, described the resulting desolation in what became northern Xinjiang as "an empty plain for a thousand <i>li</i>, with no trace of man". A fort was built (either in 1755 or 1758 depending on sources), and the Qing then established garrisons of Manchu and Mongol <a href="/wiki/Eight_Banners" title="Eight Banners">bannermen</a> and Han Chinese troops at Ürümqi.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> After 1759 state farms were also established in the vicinity of Urumchi, where there was fertile, well-watered land and few people."<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Manchus began to construct a walled city in 1763 to the south of the first fort, and it was completed in 1767.<sup id="cite_ref-piper_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-piper-4">[4]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Qianlong_Emperor" title="Qianlong Emperor">Qianlong Emperor</a> had named the new settlement "Dihua" (Chinese: <span lang="zh-Hans" xml:lang="zh-Hans">迪化</span>; pinyin: <i><span lang="zh-Latn-pinyin" xml:lang="zh-Latn-pinyin">Díhuà</span></i>; <a href="/wiki/Manchu_language" title="Manchu language">Manchu</a>: <i>Wen de dahabure fu</i>), meaning "to enlighten".<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> In 1771, another city named Gongning Cheng (鞏寧城) was built to the northwest to house Manchu bannermen, and this would become the seat of government.<sup id="cite_ref-piper_4-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-piper-4">[4]</a></sup> The bannermen settlement to the west was commonly referred to as Mancheng (滿城, Manchu City), while Dihua to the east became a Han Chinese town commonly called Hancheng (Han City).<sup id="cite_ref-jeong_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jeong-11">[11]</a></sup> The Ürümqi of the early period was therefore a <a href="/wiki/Twin_cities" title="Twin cities">twin-city</a>, with Gongning Cheng the administrative center while Dihua grew into Xinjiang's commercial and financial center.<sup id="cite_ref-Millward_1998_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Millward_1998-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>Chinese <a href="/wiki/Hui_people" title="Hui people">Hui Muslims</a> from <a href="/wiki/Gansu" title="Gansu">Gansu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shaanxi" title="Shaanxi">Shaanxi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Han_Chinese" title="Han Chinese">Han Chinese</a> from all over China began to move into Dihua.<sup id="cite_ref-Millward1998_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Millward1998-13">[13]</a></sup> By 1762, more than 500 shops had already been opened by Chinese migrants to the area of modern-day Ürümqi. Those Qing literati who visited Dihua were impressed by its cultural sophistication and similarity to eastern China. The writer <a href="/wiki/Ji_Xiaolan" class="mw-redirect" title="Ji Xiaolan">Ji Xiaolan</a> compared Dihua to Beijing, in that both had numerous wine shops which offered daily performances of Chinese music and dance.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> The origin of Hui in Urumqi is often indicated by the names of their Mosques.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi_(1870)" title="Battle of Ürümqi (1870)">Battle of Ürümqi</a> took place in 1870 between the Turkic Muslim forces of <a href="/wiki/Yaqub_Beg" title="Yaqub Beg">Yaqub Beg</a> against the <a href="/wiki/Hui_people" title="Hui people">Dungan Muslim</a> forces of Tuo Ming (Daud Khalifa). With the help of Xu Xuegong's <a href="/wiki/Han_Chinese" title="Han Chinese">Han Chinese</a> militia, Yaqub Beg's forces defeated the Dungans.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> Gongning Cheng was captured, its Qing administrator killed, and the city burnt to the ground and abandoned.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> The Qing later regained control of Ürümqi. In 1884, the <a href="/wiki/Guangxu_Emperor" title="Guangxu Emperor">Guangxu Emperor</a> established <a href="/wiki/Xinjiang" title="Xinjiang">Xinjiang</a> as a Province, with Dihua as its capital.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Republican_era">Republican era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Republican era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After the collapse of the Qing dynasty, Xinjiang was ruled from Ürümqi by a succession of warlords: <a href="/wiki/Yang_Zengxin" title="Yang Zengxin">Yang Zengxin</a> (1911–1928), <a href="/wiki/Jin_Shuren" title="Jin Shuren">Jin Shuren</a> (1928–1933), and <a href="/wiki/Sheng_Shicai" title="Sheng Shicai">Sheng Shicai</a> (1933–1942), finally <a href="/wiki/Zhang_Zhizhong" title="Zhang Zhizhong">Zhang Zhizhong</a> as governor of Xinjiang in 1942–1949. Of these, Yang and Zheng were considered capable rulers.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Kumul_Rebellion" title="Kumul Rebellion">Kumul Rebellion</a> the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi_(1933)" title="Battle of Ürümqi (1933)">Battle of Ürümqi (1933)</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi_(1933%E2%80%9334)" title="Battle of Ürümqi (1933–34)">Battle of Ürümqi (1933–34)</a> took place between the forces of <a href="/wiki/Ma_Zhongying" title="Ma Zhongying">Ma Zhongying</a>'s <a href="/wiki/36th_Division_(National_Revolutionary_Army)" title="36th Division (National Revolutionary Army)">36th Division (National Revolutionary Army)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jin_Shuren" title="Jin Shuren">Jin Shuren</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sheng_Shicai" title="Sheng Shicai">Sheng Shicai</a>'s provincial forces. At the second battle Ma was assisted by the <a href="/wiki/Han_Chinese" title="Han Chinese">Han Chinese</a> General <a href="/wiki/Zhang_Peiyuan" title="Zhang Peiyuan">Zhang Peiyuan</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="People.27s_Republic_era">People's Republic era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: People's Republic era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Following the founding of the People's Republic of China, on 1 February 1954, the city's name was officially changed back to its Dzungar Oirat name <b>Ürümqi</b>, meaning "beautiful pasture" in the <a href="/wiki/Oirat_language" title="Oirat language">Oirat language</a> of the Dzungar people.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the late 1970s, <a href="/wiki/Deng_Xiaoping" title="Deng Xiaoping">Deng Xiaoping</a> relaxed China's tight control over Xinjiang, which led to a boom of Ürümqi from the development of oil and gas industry in Xinjiang.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>New, big mosques have been financially assisted in being built by the Chinese government in Urumqi.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> While in southern Xinjiang China implements strong rules regarding religion, in Urumqi, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> treats the Uyghurs and religion lax and permissively.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>The city suffered from a series of unrest, In May 1989, <a href="/wiki/1989_%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi_unrest" title="1989 Ürümqi unrest">unrest in Ürümqi</a> resulted in 150 injuries. In February 1997, bombings in Ürümqi following the <a href="/wiki/Ghulja_incident" title="Ghulja incident">Ghulja incident</a> resulted in 20 deaths and scores of injuries.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="July_2009_riots_and_subsequent_unrest">July 2009 riots and subsequent unrest</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: July 2009 riots and subsequent unrest">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/July_2009_%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi_riots" title="July 2009 Ürümqi riots">July 2009 Ürümqi riots</a> and <a href="/wiki/September_2009_Xinjiang_unrest" title="September 2009 Xinjiang unrest">September 2009 Xinjiang unrest</a></div>
<p>In the largest eruption of ethnic violence in China in decades, major rioting broke out in July 2009 between ethnic Han Chinese and Uyghurs. The <i>New York Times</i> reporter covering the riot described the violence as "clashes with riot police and Uighurs rampaging through the city and killing Han civilians. Then, for at least three days, bands of Han vigilantes roamed Urumqi, attacking and killing Uighurs."<sup id="cite_ref-nyt_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-28">[28]</a></sup> Before the riot broke out, young Uighurs had marched through the city "to protest a case of judicial discrimination".<sup id="cite_ref-nyt_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-28">[28]</a></sup> According to official figures, most of the 197 killed in the riot were Han, a statement disputed by Uighurs.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt_28-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-28">[28]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-deathtooll_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-deathtooll-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The largest city in <a href="/wiki/Western_China" title="Western China">western China</a>, Ürümqi has earned a place in the <i><a href="/wiki/Guinness_Book_of_Records" class="mw-redirect" title="Guinness Book of Records">Guinness Book of Records</a></i> as the most remote city from any sea in the world. It is about 2,500 kilometres (1,600&#160;mi) from the nearest coastline as Ürümqi is the closest major city to the Eurasian <a href="/wiki/Pole_of_inaccessibility" title="Pole of inaccessibility">pole of inaccessibility</a>, although <a href="/wiki/Karamay" title="Karamay">Karamay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Altay_City" title="Altay City">Altay</a>, both in Xinjiang, are closer.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> The city has an administrative area of 10,989 square kilometres (4,243&#160;sq&#160;mi) and has an average elevation of 800 metres (2,600&#160;ft).</p>
<p>The location <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi&amp;params=43_40_52_N_87_19_52_E_"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">43°40′52″N</span> <span class="longitude">87°19′52″E</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">﻿ / ﻿</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">43.68111°N 87.33111°E</span><span style="display:none">﻿ / <span class="geo">43.68111; 87.33111</span></span></span></a></span> in the southwestern suburbs of Ürümqi (<a href="/wiki/%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi_County" title="Ürümqi County">Ürümqi County</a>) was designated by local geography experts as the "center point of Asia" in 1992, and a <a href="/wiki/Geographical_Center_of_Asian_Continent" class="mw-redirect" title="Geographical Center of Asian Continent">monument to this effect</a> was erected there in the 1990s. The site is a local tourist attraction.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Water_supply">Water supply</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Water supply">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Although surrounded by deserts (the <a href="/wiki/Gurbant%C3%BCngg%C3%BCt_Desert" title="Gurbantünggüt Desert">Gurbantünggüt</a> in the north and the <a href="/wiki/Taklamakan_Desert" title="Taklamakan Desert">Taklamakan</a> in the south), the Ürümqi area is naturally watered by a number of small rivers flowing from the snow-capped <a href="/wiki/Tian_Shan" title="Tian Shan">Tian Shan</a> mountains: the main range of the Tian Shan in south of the city (<a href="/wiki/%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi_County" title="Ürümqi County">Ürümqi County</a>), and the <a href="/wiki/Bogda_Shan" title="Bogda Shan">Bogda Shan</a> east of the city (<a href="/wiki/Dabancheng_District" title="Dabancheng District">Dabancheng District</a>). A network of small reservoirs and canals redistribute the water throughout the extensively irrigated area along the foothills of the mountain ranges.</p>
<p>As the Ürümqi region's population and economy is growing, the water demand exceeds the natural supply. To alleviate water shortages, the <a href="/wiki/Irtysh%E2%80%93Karamay%E2%80%93%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi_Canal" title="Irtysh–Karamay–Ürümqi Canal">Irtysh–Ürümqi Canal</a> was constructed in the first decade of the 21st century. The canal's main trunk terminates in the so-called "Reservoir 500" ("500"水库; <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi&amp;params=44_12_00_N_87_49_00_E_region:CN-62_type:landmark"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">44°12′00″N</span> <span class="longitude">87°49′00″E</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">﻿ / ﻿</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">44.20000°N 87.81667°E</span><span style="display:none">﻿ / <span class="geo">44.20000; 87.81667</span></span></span></a></span>) in the far north-eastern suburbs of the city (on the border of Ürümqi's suburban <a href="/wiki/Midong_District" title="Midong District">Midong District</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fukang" title="Fukang">Fukang</a> City). A new industrial area, called Ganquanbao Industrial Park (甘泉堡工业园), or Industrial New City 500 (500工业新城) was being developed in 2009, west of the reservoir, relying on it for water supply.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> From the reservoir area water is further distributed over a network of canals throughout the lower Midong District.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Ürümqi a <a href="/wiki/Semi-arid_climate" title="Semi-arid climate">semi-arid climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Semi-arid_climate#Cold_Semi-arid_climates" title="Semi-arid climate">BSk</a></i>) prevails, with very large differences between summer and winter, warm summers, with a July daily average of 23.7&#160;°C (74.7&#160;°F), and very cold winters, with a January daily average of −12.6&#160;°C (9.3&#160;°F). The annual average temperature is 6.90&#160;°C (44.4&#160;°F). The city is semi-arid, with its summers slightly wetter than its winters, yet sunny weather is much more likely in the warmer months, and relative humidity is the lowest during summer. With monthly percent possible sunshine ranging from 30&#160;percent in December to 70&#160;percent in August and September, the city receives 2,523 hours of bright sunshine annually. Its annual precipitation is about 290 millimetres (11.4&#160;in). Extremes since 1951 have ranged from −41.5&#160;°C (−43&#160;°F) on 27 February 1951 to 42.1&#160;°C (108&#160;°F) on 1 August 1973.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air_quality_and_pollution">Air quality and pollution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Air quality and pollution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Ambox_current_red.svg" class="image"><img alt="Ambox current red.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png" width="42" height="34" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="360" data-file-height="290" /></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section needs to be <b>updated</b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span> <small><i>(November 2015)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>According to the National Environmental Analysis released by <a href="/wiki/Tsinghua_University" title="Tsinghua University">Tsinghua University</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Asian_Development_Bank" title="Asian Development Bank">Asian Development Bank</a> in January 2013, Urumqi is among the top ten cities in the world with the most air pollution. According to this report, seven of these cities are in China, including <a href="/wiki/Taiyuan" title="Taiyuan">Taiyuan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lanzhou" title="Lanzhou">Lanzhou</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chongqing" title="Chongqing">Chongqing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jinan" title="Jinan">Jinan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Shijiazhuang" title="Shijiazhuang">Shijiazhuang</a> (besides Ürümqi).<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Blacksmith_Institute" class="mw-redirect" title="Blacksmith Institute">Blacksmith Institute</a> mentioned Urumqi in <i>2007 World’s Worst Polluted Places</i> caused by air pollution along with <a href="/wiki/Linfen" title="Linfen">Linfen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lanzhou" title="Lanzhou">Lanzhou</a>, all in China.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> In 2008, <i><a href="/wiki/Toronto_Star" title="Toronto Star">Toronto Star</a></i> listed Ürümqi as one of the Top Ten worst places to live in the world due to sulphurous pollution.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> Heavy haze is extremely common in winter, which frequently affects air traffic. Officials believed that severe winter air pollution in Ürümqi is mainly caused by energy-heavy industries and the outdated coal-firing winter heating system.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> According to a report by Department of Environmental Science and Engineering of <a href="/wiki/Fudan_University" title="Fudan University">Fudan University</a>, the average PM<sub>2.5</sub> and TSP concentrations in the winter of 2007 were 12 times higher than USA standard for PM<sub>2.5</sub> and 3 times the National Ambient Air Quality Standard of China for TSP.<sup id="cite_ref-fudan_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fudan-40">[40]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Sulfur_dioxide" title="Sulfur dioxide">sulfur dioxide</a> from industrial emissions mixed with the local anthropogenic aerosol with the transported soil dust from outside the city was the main sources of the high concentration of sulfate, one of the main factors causing the heavy air pollution over Urumqi.<sup id="cite_ref-fudan_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fudan-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Timing_of_sunrise">Timing of sunrise</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Timing of sunrise">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Because of its far western location to Beijing, the sun is 2 hours and 10 minutes behind <a href="/wiki/China_Standard_Time" class="mw-redirect" title="China Standard Time">China Standard Time</a> (CST = <a href="/wiki/UTC" class="mw-redirect" title="UTC">UTC</a>+8). During early January the sun does not rise until 09:45 and it sets between 18:45 and 19:10 local time. In September and March the sun rises around 08:00, and sets around 19:45. However, in June the sun rises at about 06:25 and does not set until 21:45.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Ürümqi currently comprises 8 <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China#County_level" class="mw-redirect" title="Administrative divisions of the People's Republic of China">county-level</a> subdivisions: 7 <a href="/wiki/District_(PRC)" class="mw-redirect" title="District (PRC)">districts</a> and 1 <a href="/wiki/County_(People%27s_Republic_of_China)" class="mw-redirect" title="County (People's Republic of China)">county</a>.</p>

<td><span class="script-arabic script-Arab" dir="rtl" style="font-family:'Noto Naskh Arabic',Harmattan,Scheherazade,Lateef,Alkalami,Amiri,FreeSerif,Arial,'Times New Roman','Droid Arabic Naskh','Microsoft Sans Serif','Segoe UI','Sakkal Majalla','Microsoft Uighur','Arabic Typesetting',sans-serif,serif; font-size: 125%; font-weight:normal;">ئۈرۈمچى ناھىيىسى‎</span></td>
<td><span title="Uyghur transliteration" class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none">Ürümchi Nahiyisi</span></td>

</tr>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Ürümqi has been a multi-ethnic city from the time of the Qing conquest; in the early years, the Manchus lived in Gongning Cheng, Han Chinese in Dihua, and various other ethnic groups such as the Hui, Uyghurs and others in the suburban districts.<sup id="cite_ref-piper2_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-piper2-42">[42]</a></sup> The Muslims settled to the south of the walled-city of Dihua, and although the walls have since been demolishded, the Muslims are still concentrated there.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> A census of in 1787 showed that there were 114,348 Hui and Han in the prefectures of Zhenxi (which included Barköl and Hami) and Ürümqi.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> In Ürümqi city itself, there were 39,000 people in the 1880s, and by the early 20th century, 50,000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-piper2_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-piper2-42">[42]</a></sup> Ürümqi in 1908 was said to have been inhabited by Uyghurs (then called Turkis), Chinese, Manchus and a few Mongols, with the Uyghurs estimated to comprise a quarter of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the People's Republic era, an active program to resettle Han population in Xinjiang was initiated.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> In 1960, there were 76,496 Uyghurs and 477,321 Han in Urumqi.<sup id="cite_ref-Millward2007_2_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Millward2007_2-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to the 2000 census, Ürümqi had 2,081,834 inhabitants, with a population density of 174.53 inhabitants/km<sup>2</sup> (452.3 inhabitants/sq. mi.).<sup id="cite_ref-2000_census_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2000_census-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the 2010 census, the population was recorded as 3,112,559. Part of the increase is due to boundary changes, for example, <a href="/wiki/Miquan" title="Miquan">Miquan</a> was merged into <a href="/wiki/Midong_District" title="Midong District">Midong District</a> and became part of Ürümqi in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Outer_Ring_Road_of_Urumqi.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Outer_Ring_Road_of_Urumqi.jpg/250px-Outer_Ring_Road_of_Urumqi.jpg" width="250" height="175" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Outer_Ring_Road_of_Urumqi.jpg/375px-Outer_Ring_Road_of_Urumqi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Outer_Ring_Road_of_Urumqi.jpg/500px-Outer_Ring_Road_of_Urumqi.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1983" data-file-height="1386" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Outer_Ring_Road_of_Urumqi.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Outer Ring Road viaducts in Urumqi at night</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Ürümqi is a major industrial center within Xinjiang. Ürümqi, together with <a href="/wiki/Karamay" title="Karamay">Karamay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Korla" title="Korla">Korla</a>, account for 64.5&#160;percent of the total industrial output of Xinjiang. Ürümqi is also the largest consumer center in the region, recording <a href="/wiki/Renminbi" title="Renminbi">¥</a>41.9 billion retail sales of consumer goods in 2008, an increase of 26&#160;percent from 2007. The <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">GDP</a> per capita reached US$6,222 in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> According to statistics, Urumqi ranked 7th in 2008 by the disposable income for urban residents among cities in <a href="/wiki/Western_China" title="Western China">Western China</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> Ürümqi has been a central developmental target for the <a href="/wiki/China_Western_Development" title="China Western Development">China Western Development</a> project that the Central Government is pursuing.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Urumqi_Foreign_Economic_Relations_and_Trade_Fair" title="Urumqi Foreign Economic Relations and Trade Fair">Urumqi Foreign Economic Relations and Trade Fair</a> (<a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese</a>: <span lang="zh" xml:lang="zh">乌洽会</span>) has been held annually since 1991 and has been upgraded into the first <a href="/wiki/China-Eurasia_Expo" title="China-Eurasia Expo">China-Eurasia Expo</a> in 2011. Its purpose is to promote domestic and foreign markets. The 17th Fair has attracted participants from the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Commerce_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Ministry of Commerce of the People's Republic of China">Ministry of Commerce</a> and the <a href="/wiki/China_Council_for_the_Promotion_of_International_Trade" title="China Council for the Promotion of International Trade">China Council for Promotion of International Trade</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Urumqi_partial_panorama_at_dusk.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Urumqi_partial_panorama_at_dusk.JPG/250px-Urumqi_partial_panorama_at_dusk.JPG" width="250" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Urumqi_partial_panorama_at_dusk.JPG/375px-Urumqi_partial_panorama_at_dusk.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Urumqi_partial_panorama_at_dusk.JPG/500px-Urumqi_partial_panorama_at_dusk.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Urumqi_partial_panorama_at_dusk.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Buildings in Urumqi CBDs near <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Square_(%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi)" title="People's Square (Ürümqi)">People's Square</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Xinjiang Guanghui Group (新疆广汇集团) is the largest <a href="/wiki/Real_estate" title="Real estate">real estate</a> enterprise and most powerful <a href="/wiki/Privately_held_company" title="Privately held company">privately owned company</a> in Xinjiang and is currently engaged in energy and automobile. <a href="/wiki/Zhong_Tian_Plaza" title="Zhong Tian Plaza">China CITIC Bank Mansion</a> (中信银行大厦), headquarters of Guanghui, located in one of the CBDs in North Xinhua Road, is the tallest building in Urumqi and <a href="/wiki/Xinjiang" title="Xinjiang">Xinjiang</a>; with a height of 229 metres, it is also the tallest in <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Northwestern China">Northwestern China</a> and <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a>. Zhongshan Road (Sun Yat-sen Road, Chinese: 中山路) has been one of the ten most famous commercial streets in China since 2005. Zhongshan Road has always been the hub of <a href="/wiki/Consumer_electronics" title="Consumer electronics">consumer electronics</a> in the city, with the largest computer, <a href="/wiki/Mobile_phone" title="Mobile phone">mobile phone</a> and <a href="/wiki/Consumer_electronics" title="Consumer electronics">consumer electronics</a> market in Xinjiang, including Baihuacun, Cyber Digital Plaza and Fountain Plaza.</p>
<p>As the economic center in Xinjiang, Urumqi has expanded its urban area since the 1990s. The <a href="/wiki/Central_Business_District" class="mw-redirect" title="Central Business District">CBDs</a> in the city increased rapidly all around the major districts. Despite the old city areas being primarily in the south, the development in the north part began since the late 1980s. The completion of the new office tower for Urumqi Municipal Government in 2003 at <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nanhu_Square&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Nanhu Square (page does not exist)">Nanhu Square</a> (南湖广场) in Nanhu Road marked a shift of the city center to the north. Lacking a subway, the city commenced the construction of <a href="/wiki/Viaduct" title="Viaduct">viaducts</a> for Outer Ring Road (外环路) since 2003, which considerably facilitates transport. Youhao Road (友好路) and surrounding neighborhood, is the commercial center for business, shopping and amusement. Youhao Group (友好集团), the namesake local enterprise, owns a major market share of retails. Maison Mode Urumqi (乌鲁木齐美美百货), open since 2008, became one of the few notable department stores for <a href="/wiki/Luxury_good" class="mw-redirect" title="Luxury good">luxury merchandise</a> in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> The Urumqi Economic and Technological Development Zone (UETD) located in the northern <a href="/wiki/Toutunhe_District" title="Toutunhe District">Toutunhe District</a>, has been a leading base for steel, machinery manufacturing, biochemistry and other industrial innovations.</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:People%27s_Square_of_Urumqi_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/People%27s_Square_of_Urumqi_1.jpg/220px-People%27s_Square_of_Urumqi_1.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/People%27s_Square_of_Urumqi_1.jpg/330px-People%27s_Square_of_Urumqi_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/People%27s_Square_of_Urumqi_1.jpg/440px-People%27s_Square_of_Urumqi_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="900" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:People%27s_Square_of_Urumqi_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/People%27s_Square_(%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi)" title="People's Square (Ürümqi)">People's Square</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Urumqi_s_bazzar.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Urumqi_s_bazzar.jpg/220px-Urumqi_s_bazzar.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Urumqi_s_bazzar.jpg/330px-Urumqi_s_bazzar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Urumqi_s_bazzar.jpg/440px-Urumqi_s_bazzar.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Urumqi_s_bazzar.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Grand_Bazaar_(%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi)" title="Grand Bazaar (Ürümqi)">International Grand Bazaar Xinjiang</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Grand_Bazaar_(%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi)" title="Grand Bazaar (Ürümqi)">Grand Bazaar</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Bazaar" title="Bazaar">bazaar</a> on South Jiefang Road (<span lang="zh" xml:lang="zh">解放南路</span>).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hong_Shan" title="Hong Shan">Hong Shan</a> (Red Mountain) is the symbol of Urumqi, located in Hongshan Park.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/People%27s_Park_(%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi)" title="People's Park (Ürümqi)">People's Park</a>, south of Hongshan Park.</li>
<li>Glacier No. 1 (<span lang="zh-hans" xml:lang="zh-hans">一号冰川</span>), origin of Urumqi River, is the largest glacier near a major city in China.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/People%27s_Square_(%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi)" title="People's Square (Ürümqi)">People's Square</a></li>
<li>Nanhu Square (<span lang="zh-hans" xml:lang="zh-hans">南湖广场</span>)</li>
<li>Xinjiang Uygur Autonomous Region Museum (<span lang="zh-hans" xml:lang="zh-hans">新疆维吾尔自治区博物馆</span>), which was completely rebuilt in the early 2000s.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Heaven_Lake_of_Tian_Shan" class="mw-redirect" title="Heaven Lake of Tian Shan">Heavenly Lake Scenic Area</a>, a popular park with some of China's most famous alpine scenery, a little more than two hours outside Urumqi.</li>
<li>Shuimogou Hot Springs (<span lang="zh-hans" xml:lang="zh-hans">水磨沟温泉</span>) is located 5&#160;km (3.1&#160;mi) northeast of Urumqi.</li>
<li>Xinjiang Silk Road Museum (<span lang="zh-hans" xml:lang="zh-hans">新疆丝绸之路博物馆</span>) is located right next to the Grand Bazaar at No. 160 Shengli Road. It is located on the fourth and fifth floor of a very large European style building which houses a shopping complex as well. Most of the exhibits have English names as well and some of their guides speak some English.</li>
<li>Ürümqi City Museum (<span lang="zh-hans" xml:lang="zh-hans">乌鲁木齐博物馆</span>) is located at South Nanhu Road 123 (<span lang="zh-hans" xml:lang="zh-hans">南湖南路123号</span>).</li>
<li>Urumqi Tartar <a href="/wiki/Mosque" title="Mosque">Mosque</a> (<span lang="zh-hans" xml:lang="zh-hans">乌鲁木齐塔塔尔寺清真寺</span>) is a luxuriously furbished mosque located on Jiefang Road. The mosque is open to female and male visitors unlike other mosques. However, permission must have been obtained prior to visiting the mosque.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></li>
<li>The monument at the <a href="/wiki/Geographical_Center_of_Asian_Continent" class="mw-redirect" title="Geographical Center of Asian Continent">Geographical Center of Asian Continent</a>, in Yongfeng Township, <a href="/wiki/%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi_County" title="Ürümqi County">Ürümqi County</a></li>
<li>Xinjiang International Grand Bazaar in Urumqi City Tianshan District, which is currently the country's largest bazaar. The architectural style of the Grand Bazaar grand scale and very Islamic style, bazaar inside the market characteristics of ethnic minorities commodity dazzling, rich and exquisite. International Grand Bazaar in Urumqi in most ethnic customs, visitors came to Urumqi play will come to see</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education_and_science">Education and science</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Education and science">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Xife.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d1/Xife.jpg/220px-Xife.jpg" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d1/Xife.jpg/330px-Xife.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d1/Xife.jpg/440px-Xife.jpg 2x" data-file-width="468" data-file-height="320" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Xife.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Xinjiang University of Finance and Economics.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Front-Gate_of_Urumqi_No.1_High_School.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Front-Gate_of_Urumqi_No.1_High_School.JPG/220px-Front-Gate_of_Urumqi_No.1_High_School.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Front-Gate_of_Urumqi_No.1_High_School.JPG/330px-Front-Gate_of_Urumqi_No.1_High_School.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Front-Gate_of_Urumqi_No.1_High_School.JPG/440px-Front-Gate_of_Urumqi_No.1_High_School.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">

<p>Urumqi has many educational campuses including <a href="/wiki/Xinjiang_University" title="Xinjiang University">Xinjiang University</a>, Xinjiang Normal University, <a href="/wiki/Xinjiang_Agricultural_University" title="Xinjiang Agricultural University">Xinjiang Agricultural University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Xinjiang_Medical_University" title="Xinjiang Medical University">Xinjiang Medical University</a> and many others.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air">Air</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Air">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Ürümqi is served by the <a href="/wiki/%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi_Diwopu_International_Airport" title="Ürümqi Diwopu International Airport">Ürümqi Diwopu International Airport</a>. It is a hub for China Southern Airlines. Ürümqi Diwopu International Airport is the largest airport in Xinjiang.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">Rail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Rail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Ürümqi is Xinjiang's main rail hub with two primary railway stations, the long-standing <a href="/wiki/%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi_South_Railway_Station" title="Ürümqi South Railway Station">Ürümqi South Railway Station</a> (formerly the Urumqi Railway Station) and <a href="/wiki/%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi_Railway_Station" title="Ürümqi Railway Station">Ürümqi Railway Station</a> opened in July 2016. The <a href="/wiki/Lanxin_High-Speed_Railway" class="mw-redirect" title="Lanxin High-Speed Railway">a high-speed rail line</a> connects both stations, running from Ürümqi to <a href="/wiki/Lanzhou" title="Lanzhou">Lanzhou</a> which has been in operation since the end of 2014.</p>
<p>The city is served by several conventional rail lines. Ürümqi is the western terminus of the <a href="/wiki/Lanzhou%E2%80%93Xinjiang_Railway" title="Lanzhou–Xinjiang Railway">Lanzhou–Xinjiang (Lanxin)</a> and <a href="/wiki/%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi%E2%80%93Dzungaria_Railway" title="Ürümqi–Dzungaria Railway">Ürümqi–Dzungaria (Wuzhun)</a> Railway, and the eastern terminus of the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Xinjiang_Railway" title="Northern Xinjiang Railway">Northern Xinjiang (Beijiang)</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Second_%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi%E2%80%93Jinghe_Railway" title="Second Ürümqi–Jinghe Railway">Second Ürümqi–Jinghe Railway</a>. The Beijiang and the Lanxin Lines form part of the <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_Land_Bridge" title="Eurasian Land Bridge">Trans-Eurasian Continental Railway</a>, which runs from <a href="/wiki/Rotterdam" title="Rotterdam">Rotterdam</a> through the <a href="/wiki/Dzungarian_Gate" title="Dzungarian Gate">Alataw Pass</a> on the Kazakhstan border to Ürümqi and on to Lanzhou and <a href="/wiki/Lianyungang" title="Lianyungang">Lianyungang</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Road">Road</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Road">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/China_National_Highway_216" title="China National Highway 216">China National Highway 216</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/China_National_Highway_312" title="China National Highway 312">China National Highway 312</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/China_National_Highway_314" title="China National Highway 314">China National Highway 314</a></li>
</ul>
<p>Many roads to the north and west typically shut down by early October, remaining closed until the end of winter.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Metro">Metro</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Metro">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi_Metro" title="Ürümqi Metro">Ürümqi Metro</a> is under construction with plans submitted for 7 lines totalling 211.9 kilometres (131.7 miles) in length with an estimated cost of 31.24 billion yuan.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since March 20, 2014 Line 1 has been under construction and is expected to open in 2019. The line will connect <a href="/wiki/%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi_Diwopu_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Ürümqi Diwopu Airport">Ürümqi Diwopu Airport</a> through downtown Ürümqi and end at the Southern Long Distance Bus Station (南郊客运站) with a total length of 26.5 kilometres (16.5 miles) and 21 stations (16 underground, 5 elevated).<sup id="cite_ref-1begin_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1begin-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bus_rapid_transit">Bus rapid transit</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Bus rapid transit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi_BRT" title="Ürümqi BRT">Ürümqi BRT</a> bus service was launched in August 2011 after an investment of 930 million yuan in an effort to improve urban traffic.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> There are currently four routes operated, BRT1, BRT2, BRT3, and BRT5 mainly along the north-to-south downtown major roads.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Urumqi_UTV_logo.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/42/Urumqi_UTV_logo.svg/120px-Urumqi_UTV_logo.svg.png" width="120" height="97" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/42/Urumqi_UTV_logo.svg/180px-Urumqi_UTV_logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/42/Urumqi_UTV_logo.svg/240px-Urumqi_UTV_logo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="482" data-file-height="391" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Urumqi_UTV_logo.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Logo of Urumqi Television Station, shaped after <a href="/wiki/Hong_Shan" title="Hong Shan">Hong Shan</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Xinjiang_Networking_Transmission_Limited" title="Xinjiang Networking Transmission Limited">Xinjiang Networking Transmission Limited</a> operates the <a href="/wiki/Urumqi_People%27s_Broadcasting_Station" title="Urumqi People's Broadcasting Station">Urumqi People's Broadcasting Station</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Xinjiang_People_Broadcasting_Station" class="mw-redirect" title="Xinjiang People Broadcasting Station">Xinjiang People Broadcasting Station</a>, broadcasting in the <a href="/wiki/Standard_Chinese" title="Standard Chinese">Mandarin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uyghur_language" title="Uyghur language">Uyghur</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kazakh_language" title="Kazakh language">Kazakh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mongolian_language" title="Mongolian language">Mongolian</a>, Russian and the <a href="/wiki/Kyrgyz_language" title="Kyrgyz language">Kyrgyz</a> languages.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Xinjiang_Television_Station" class="mw-redirect" title="Xinjiang Television Station">Xinjiang Television Station</a> (XJTV), located in Urumqi, is the major TV broadcasting station in the <a href="/wiki/Xinjiang_Uyghur_Autonomous_Region" class="mw-redirect" title="Xinjiang Uyghur Autonomous Region">Xinjiang Uyghur Autonomous Region</a>. The local television station for Urumqi city is <a href="/wiki/Urumqi_Television_Station" class="mw-redirect" title="Urumqi Television Station">Urumqi Television Station</a> (UTV)(乌鲁木齐电视台).</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Xinjiang_Flying_Tigers" title="Xinjiang Flying Tigers">Xinjiang Flying Tigers</a> or <a href="/w/index.php?title=Guanghui_Flying_Tigers&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Guanghui Flying Tigers (page does not exist)">Guanghui Flying Tigers</a> is a major basketball team that is part of the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Basketball_Association" title="Chinese Basketball Association">Chinese Basketball Association</a>, based in Ürümqi, Xinjiang. Its corporate sponsor is Xinjiang Guanghui Group</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Xinjiang_Tianshan_Leopard_F.C." title="Xinjiang Tianshan Leopard F.C.">Xinjiang Tianshan Leopard F.C.</a> is a local football team in the <a href="/wiki/China_League_One" title="China League One">China League One</a></li>
</ul>
<p>China started a <a href="/wiki/Bandy" title="Bandy">bandy</a> development programme by organising educational days in Ürümqi in June 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2015 an indoor <a href="/wiki/Speed_skating" title="Speed skating">speed skating</a> arena was opened.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>

<div style="padding:0em 0.25em"></div>
<table class="nowraplinks collapsible collapsed navbox-subgroup" style="border-spacing:0">
<tr>
<th scope="col" class="navbox-title" colspan="2" style=";"><span style="float:left;width:6em">&#160;</span>
<div id="Notes" style="font-size:114%"><small>Notes</small></div>
</th>
</tr>
<tr style="height:2px">
<td colspan="2"></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" class="navbox-list navbox-odd" style="width:100%;padding:0px">
<div style="padding:0em 0.25em"></div>
<table class="nowraplinks navbox-subgroup" style="border-spacing:0">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" class="navbox-list navbox-odd" style="width:100%;padding:0px">
<div style="padding:0em 0.25em">* Indicates this city has already occurred above.<br />
<p><sup>a</sup><a href="/wiki/Direct-controlled_municipality_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Direct-controlled municipality of China">Direct-controlled Municipalities</a>. <sup>b</sup><a href="/wiki/Sub-provincial_city_in_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Sub-provincial city in the People's Republic of China">Sub-provincial cities as provincial capitals</a>. <sup>c</sup><a href="/wiki/Sub-provincial_city_in_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Sub-provincial city in the People's Republic of China">Separate state-planning cities</a>. <sup>1</sup><a href="/wiki/Special_Economic_Zones_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Special Economic Zones of China">Special Economic Zone Cities</a>. <sup>2</sup><a href="/wiki/Special_Economic_Zones_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Special Economic Zones of China">Coastal development cities</a>.<br />
<sup>3</sup>Prefecture capital status established by Heilongjiang Province and not recognized by Ministry of Civil Affairs. Disputed by <a href="/wiki/Oroqen_Autonomous_Banner" title="Oroqen Autonomous Banner">Oroqen Autonomous Banner</a>, Hulunbuir, Inner Mongolia as part of it.<br />
<sup>4</sup>Only administers islands and waters in South China Sea and have no urban core comparable to typical cities in China.<br />
<sup>5</sup>The claimed province of <a href="/wiki/Taiwan_Province,_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Taiwan Province, People's Republic of China">Taiwan</a> no longer have any internal division announced by Ministry of Civil Affairs of PRC, due to lack of actual jurisdiction. See <a href="/wiki/Template:Administrative_divisions_of_the_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Template:Administrative divisions of the Republic of China">Template:Administrative divisions of the Republic of China</a> instead.<br /></p>
All provincial capitals are listed first in prefecture-level cities by province.</div>
</td>
</tr>
